<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1340779237">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1340779237" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/968378-marcy-dermansky" class="left imgcol" title="Marcy Dermansky"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442461311p2/968378.jpg" alt="Marcy Dermansky" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1340779237?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 20, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/968378-marcy-dermansky" class="user" title="Marcy Dermansky">Marcy Dermansky</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1340779237">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2708622041037604310">I bought this at a used bookstore for three dollars, happy to discover an old Ellen Gilchrist novel I had never read before. It turned out this was so much like so many Ellen Gilchrist short stories, and Sarah Conley was Rhoda and Nora and so many other Gilchrist heroines turned into one, and Sarah Conley gets to go to Paris and eat incredible food and wear incredible clothes and fly on the Concorde as if was nothing (yes this book is dated) and she is the editor at Time and has an agent who mak</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2708622041037604310">I bought this at a used bookstore for three dollars, happy to discover an old Ellen Gilchrist novel I had never read before. It turned out this was so much like so many Ellen Gilchrist short stories, and Sarah Conley was Rhoda and Nora and so many other Gilchrist heroines turned into one, and Sarah Conley gets to go to Paris and eat incredible food and wear incredible clothes and fly on the Concorde as if was nothing (yes this book is dated) and she is the editor at Time and has an agent who makes her lots of money and she gets made perfect love to on more than one occasion, and I didn't believe it all but I liked it, as far as fantasy lives goes. Fun to read. But really, what I liked how selfish Sarah Conley was, completely unflinchingly selfish. And how that was a good thing. <br /><br />Here is a passage that stood out for me. "I have worked all my life to fix it so I could be with healthy people, Sarah told herself. With people who work, people are successful at what they do. And I will stay with them. I will not enter into the unhealthy madness of anyone, not even my own family." </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_312075075">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/312075075" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/333860-marissa-morrison" class="left imgcol" title="Marissa Morrison"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1198338757p2/333860.jpg" alt="Marissa Morrison" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/312075075?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 13, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/333860-marissa-morrison" class="user" title="Marissa Morrison">Marissa Morrison</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer312075075">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15552877661978827435">About a third of the way into this book, I remembered that I'd read it 10 years ago. So I knew some of the key plot points. I've always loved Gilchrist's spunky female characters and sprawling plots. However, this book seemed way too long for the action contained within it. Also, I was struck by how unpolished Gilchrist's writing is--simple sentence structure, everyday words, terse dialogue. It seems that if a writer isn't using words to really describe anything, then her style ought to be tweak</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15552877661978827435">About a third of the way into this book, I remembered that I'd read it 10 years ago. So I knew some of the key plot points. I've always loved Gilchrist's spunky female characters and sprawling plots. However, this book seemed way too long for the action contained within it. Also, I was struck by how unpolished Gilchrist's writing is--simple sentence structure, everyday words, terse dialogue. It seems that if a writer isn't using words to really describe anything, then her style ought to be tweaked. For instance, at one point a character gets drunk and embarrasses herself, causing her relatives to worry about her mental health. Gilchrist does not describe the drunkenness, only says that the character got drunk. Since there are, of course, many ways of being inebriated and making a fool of one's self, I had a hard time picturing what had happened in this scene. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15552877661978827435">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I was prejudiced in Gilchrist's favor for another reason: I attended an Iowa Gilchrist family reunion every single June in my youth. My grandmother was a Gilchrist!!<br /><br />This book is a complete nap inducing bore. Anybody who wants it, just let me know: it's not going in the 'must keep' collection.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1442440.Sarah_Conley" title="Hardcover 9780316314770" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer15677222">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17195877665792704013">This is classic Ellen Gilchrist. If you like her short stories you're apt to enjoy this novel. It is not heavy reading, yet has intriguing characters, a plot that moves, and insights into the human condition. <br /><br />If you enjoy Paris, or even just reading about it, then that is a leg up on additional pleasure from reading this book. <br /><br />Gilchrist specializes in quirky characters who come to life on the page, as well as dialogue that always reads as conversation. She's one of my favorites. <br /><br />-- Paul</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2591221739898412966">I just keep reading Ellen Gilchrist, and I'm not exactly sure why. This one was along those same lines. It was decent entertainment, anyway.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('U350yZWEZfwhJ+7azQVYyUhWjZQ2KO4TuRxfGag7pdg2qksaZ1ZxBq3/mmGzZL57AaFOjX/1qbnTFVqLZK5TnQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('EXB+XYWtfKvjUM6Z0UnjAtyUd/Y0RFZeKKje/UDjett0pEGOd39oUW+IuiKvKAWwlWO0732ZEfRCodtvjHaMng==')})
  }

(a reference to Bunuel\'s Un Chien Andalou) serves as his ill-tempered guide.\nIn a series of vignettes, gags, illustrations, text pieces, and dream stories, ping-ponging back between the surrealist world and the &amp;quot;real&amp;quot; world, Bardín examines, questions, and defends his own beliefs, convictions and philosophies while tangling with the Dog and the Holy Trinity in a variety of guises (including a familiar-looking mouse with red shorts and white gloves).\nIn other stories, he imagines himself in a painting by Brueghel the Elder, tries to deal with his onanism in a productive way, is enlightened, dodges his real &amp;quot;creator&amp;quot; In The Devil\'s&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;span id=\"freeText13553595354645368843\" style=\"display:none\"&gt;Footnotes have not had it easy. Their dominance of eighteenth- and nineteenth- century literature and scholarship was both hard-won -- following many years of struggle -- and doomed, as it led to belittlement in the twentieth century. In The Devil\'s Details, Chuck Zerby playfully explores footnotes\' long and illustrious history and makes a clarion call to save them from the new world of the Internet and hypertext.  In a story that boasts a marvelous plot and a rogues\' gallery of players, Zerby examines traditional footnotes and their less-buttoned-down incarnations, as when used by pornographers. Yes, The Devil\'s Details is full of surprises: Zerby hunts down the first bona fide fully functioning footnote; unearths a multivolume history of Northumberland County, England, that uses one volume for a single footnote; and uncovers a murder plot. He even explains why footnotes are like blind dates.  Carefully researched and highly opinionated, The Devil\'s Details affirms that delight in reading can come from unexpected places.&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;a data-text-id=\"13553595354645368843\"     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/34005.Ellen_Gilchrist">About Ellen Gilchrist</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/34005.Ellen_Gilchrist"><img alt="34005" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1208809202p2/34005.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer13276226615460042198">Ellen Gilchrist (born February 20, 1935) is an American novelist, short story writer, and poet. She won a National Book Award for her 1984 collection of short stories, Victory Over Japan.<br /><br />Source: <a rel="nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ellen_Gilchrist">Wikipedia</a>.</span>
